Pluralizing the Latin suffix -us leads to -i But the word octopus is based on Greek, and the suffix -pus (foot) pluralizes to -podes. The confusion between the two has led the English language to adopt both, plus the -uses Feel free to block me for pedantry, but I'm gonna insist that while the plural of 'octopus' might be 'octopodes' (as it's a Greek word) or 'octopuses' (the anglicised version), it's definitely not 'octopi'(as it's not a Latin word). ;) I don't really care.
